I did the lightest setting the first time but was able to handle it on the third setting the second time. I did it for the third time a couple days ago on the fourth setting. I am already seeing results. I have really thick hair as I am mexican and native american. I have fair brown skin. What ever you do, do not get remotely close to your tatttoo if you have any, it hurts and will damage your tattoo. I didn&#x27;t read that far in the instructions. Caused a blister and discolored the small part that I went over. I was able to get 3 uses out of one cartidge but I was able to do both full legs, bikini, and arms during each session. To replace the cartridge is super easy, I had no issues. It&#x27;s important that you keep your skin moisturized after treatments, it&#x27;s like having a mild sunburn, skin gets dry. I do a salt scrub after a few days exfoliate the skin. I haven&#x27;t had to shave once in over a month. I use to shave my legs every other day. Well worth the time and investment.</li>

    <li> Light asian skin + dark hair &#x3D;&#x3D;&amp;#62; WORKS! I have traditionally always used a epilator to remove unwanted underarm hair, but UGH, my hair grows so fast. If I&#x27;m being diligent, I need to epilate every 2-3 days to have clear underarms. Getting annoyed, I decided to give this IPL system a try.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;To begin, there is a learning curve to using this thing. My first time using it, I was just kind of a mess and probably went over the same spots several times by accident. The next day, hair was growing back and I was totally disappointed for having spent so much money. But, I didn&#x27;t give up. To ensure that the thing was working, I shaved both pits but continued only IPL&#x27;ing one side for a more proper experiment.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now, it&#x27;s been several times (at least 4x) on the one side and 1x (my first messed up try) on my &amp;#34;control side&amp;#34;, and the results are in! The 4x+ IPL side&#x27;s hair has noticeably reduced! There is still hair growing there, b/c as you may know, hair grows at diff cycles, so I&#x27;m still probably zapping hairs that had a delayed growth cycle. Anyway, it&#x27;s definitely noticeably different on the two sides, so I&#x27;m very pleased and glad I kept at it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Also, don&#x27;t be discouraged if it&#x27;s unwieldy to use at first. As I said, learning curve. After a few times, you start getting the hang of using it. Key is to be methodical. Hold -&amp;#62; zap -&amp;#62; move down -&amp;#62; repeat. Never fully lift your hand as you&#x27;re holding the IPL b/c you&#x27;ll forget where you were.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I use it on the highest setting. It is a little bit of pain, but really not that significant. I would recommend testing the highest setting and seeing if you can tolerate it. Better results, I would imagine.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I am next going to try this on my bikini area, but I admit I&#x27;m a little scared haha. I have only ever waxed, and well, waxing is pretty easy for me and has pretty good and longish-lasting results (1-2 weeks)... but then again, 3 months does beat out 2 weeks by a lot!</li>

But part of the process is to shave, so I figured I&#x27;d just have to deal with it. I would say that after about 3 uses (again not consistently spaced apart), I have at least a 60 - 70% reduction in hair growth. The hair that remains doesn&#x27;t cause me to get razor bumps when I shave, so the hair shaft must be weaker.     <li> I did a lot of research before finally deciding to buy this unit. I read all the reviews on it. I really liked the fact that the reviews are mostly positive and I really liked the price.     <li> I did a lot of research before buying this IPL. I think it&#x27;s the best option considering price and cost of replacement cartridges. Also, it&#x27;s very important to me that it can be used worldwide in terms of voltage, not just US voltage, so I can still use it when I move.&lt;br /&gt;Now, as for ease of use, this couldn&#x27;t be easier and it&#x27;s very fast. I sit in front of the TV and in 15 min or less I&#x27;m done. In terms of pain it does hurt a little in some sensitive areas but much less than laser and for most of the process it&#x27;s pain free for me even in the highest setting.&lt;br /&gt;The reason I gave it a 4 instead of a 5 is because in terms of effectiveness I didn&#x27;t find it to work exactly as claimed. If the description hadn&#x27;t aimed so far I would have given it a 5 because in terms of hair reduction I&#x27;m very happy with the results. I have used it for 2 months, carefully following instructions, and I have seen a considerable reduction in the frequency of times I have to shave, but still very far from the 3-6 hair free months promised. For example, instead of having to shave my legs every couple of days now I have to shave once every two weeks or once every week if I want them really smooth. I think this is a pretty good result and if they had promised me this I would have still bought this item so I&#x27;m happy and would buy again.&lt;br /&gt;I recommend this product, just don&#x27;t expect too much and know also that in some body areas like the arms not even laser can remove hair completely for long.&lt;br /&gt;I big plus also is that it doesn&#x27;t hurt the skin even in the highest setting. I had some bad reactions to laser before but this didn&#x27;t even cause redness.&lt;br /&gt;It&#x27;s a good product and if you buy it, be aware that it will reduce hair growth but is not miraculous.</li>
    <li> Update 4/13&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My wife decided to use it about six months ago when I quit. She has had good results with it.  With her good results, I decided to use it again too. I assume her positive results depend on her hair type. Her hair is thinner than mine, thus \\&quot;maybe\\&quot; easier to zap???, thus kill the roots?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I am not sure if this is a permanent solution, but she use to have ingrown problems while epilating. The zapping has eliminated this problem, thus based on that alone, she loves it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Old review:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This product probably deserves two stars, because it does some-what work, but I figure people looking to buy this product will skim past the two star reviews and read the one star reviews.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I bought this in December through a Groupon promotion for $199.00 and not on Amazon. I have read the reviews here for four months before posting. I basically agree with one poster MrD that some of these reviews (Ama***123, which happens to be the very first review) are fake, but most reviews are just from people who have not used this product long enough to give a good review. People need to use this product for a few months, not a few weeks or first or second session before posting,  where their enthusiasm is clouding their judgement.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Yes it works, if it didn&#x27;t Remington would be sued. You will probably see 30% hair reduction after 3 sessions. Overall, maybe 40% to 50% reduction after a dozen or so sessions. The hair will start to grow back in probably a few weeks, not six months. The hair is just stunned, thus you will see the hair follicle on your skin.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;You have to ask yourself, what are you saving? If you shave, you will still have to continue to shave. 40% reduction for a few weeks will still leave you shaving daily. Is this worth the $250.00 price tag and $25.00 bulbs that seem to burn out at a few hundred pulses (not 1500 pulses and I am on my second bulb bought through Amazon.)? You decide.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;For the people who epilate, stay with epilating, the results are much better.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;For people who want permanent hair removal, go to a professional, it will be financially cheaper in the long run; especially when you are paying $100.00 a year for bulb replacements on a system that only give temporary results.     <li> I have been using this product for more than 2 years and have been very happy with my Remington I-Light Pro. I have white skin and thick, dark brown hair. You get much better results with the strongest setting. In the beginning, I would get some bumps a few days later. After a few uses, this got much better. For me, the I-Light did not completely remove hair for 6 months. Rather, it greatly reduces and thins the hair. Each time I use it, less hair grows back. And the more I use it, the less painful it is. Now that I have been using it for more than two years, it is nearly painless, even on the strongest setting (which I always use). Oh and how long does a cartridge last? Mine just expired after more than two years of zaps. I was zapping between one and two times a month. There was a period where I skipped more than a month of using the I-Light and a lot of my hair grew back. When I went back to using it again, it was a bit painful like it had been in the beginning. I think the reason that my hair starts growing back a few weeks later is because I have very thick, coarse, and stubborn hair. My guess is that if your hair is on the thinner side, your zaps will last longer. Even so, I am thrilled with my I-Light Pro. It takes two minutes every twoweeks and I am good to go. I did my legs this morning and I felt like I should have been wearing protective eye wear.  This was never a problem with the Tria.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Remington has a button you have to hold down to get the light to pulse.  Tria would pulse on contact--no button. Tria definitely wins out on this point, and if I could change one thing about the Remington, this would be it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I also dislike how difficult it is to reach the on/off switch on the Remington, but if it keeps my 6-year-old from switching it on accidentally, I&#x27;ll take it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Tria&#x27;s cool-down system was bothersome, as it would switch on and off during use and cause the laser to be sluggish. I get a patch here and there, but they are barely noticeable. I do not have to be as exact with shaving as I use to be, and I can definitely go longer without shaving. (I use to have to shave EVERY 24 hours, or I was looking rough. Now I can go a couple days with no problem.)&lt;br /&gt;  These are not even my full results. It will be another month or two to get through the full hair cycle, plus other hairs coming INTO cycle will start growing as well. So I won&#x27;t see a true result for at least another month. This is a process.... even professional salons will tell you the same thing. It takes time, and patience, but I am already seeing results that I am pleased with.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Tips:&lt;br /&gt;  1. Shave as close as possible. Most of the pain and heat I dealt with was where I got sloppy with my shaving. The closer, the better.&lt;br /&gt;  2. Use cocoa butter, or lotion on the areas you zap. I didn&#x27;t experience irritation or dryness, but I was pretty quick to lotion up. It just makes sense to me to lotion after IPLing.&lt;br /&gt;  3. Set aside time to do this. It would take me around an hour to do all the parts I wanted to hit-- which isn&#x27;t much time, but I needed to sit down and kind of yoga through some parts. It helped to know that I could sit on the floor, take my time, and make sure I got all the areas I wanted without interruption.&lt;br /&gt;  4. Be patient. I know it is frustrating, and I know how badly people want results (especially in the face area) but if you over-do it, you can harm yourself. Just give the system a chance to work the way it is supposed to.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;That is all I have for now. I hope this review helps. Again, leave questions if you&#x27;d like. I will do my best to answer them.plenty good, and even on a 3, this system was still kind of rough. But that is ME. My skin is sensitive, especially on my face and neck, so I expected this. Keep it flush with your skin to0 minimize this, it also wont zap till its close and has a good seal around area. Don&#x27;t shock any one spot more than recomended otherwise you will pay for it later, trust me. Otherwise I&#x27;m still on my first cartridge, I&#x27;ve used it on my underarms and (face/NOT RECOMMENDED) with good results. You can&#x27;t use this on or around your groin or by your nipples either. So this device is limited in application, keep this in mind before you buy. Otherwise enjoy.</li>

    <li> I had read the reviews before purchasing the iLight.  So, I was aware of some of the issues with this unit before purchase.  That said, there is one issue that I&#x27;d like to address first.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Bulb longevity&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The bulb appears to be a type of bright (and hot) halogen bulb.  As a result, it needs to be cooled.  Both the base of the unit and the flash gun have fans that operate continuously while the unit is in operation.  However, the one thing I have noticed is that even while the fans operate, the flash gun gets relatively hot after a large number of successive flashes.  The instructions recommend using a grid motion down the surface of the skin leaving the unit touching the skin while pressing and holding the flash button and then moving to the next grid position.  While holding the button down to activate the flash, the unit will continually flash every few seconds while the contact sensors make contact with the surface of the skin.  After a large number of flashes, this leads the flash gun getting quite hot. I believe this is one of two problems with the unit.  Basically, the fans in the flash gun are inadequate to cool the bulb between each flash.  As the bulb remains too hot, it seems to reduce the lifespan of the bulb.  The alternative is to wait longer between flashes or flash a number of times and let the flash gun cool down before starting the next grid area.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The second problem is turning the unit off. Once done with your session for the day, it&#x27;s tempting just to flip the switch to the off position.  Don&#x27;t do this.  Let the unit sit and cool down until the unit begins beeping again.  Then, turn it off.  Letting the unit adequately cool between each session and before power off seems to increase bulb longevity.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Whether we can actually get the Remington stated 1500 flashes out of the lamp is another matter, but I believe you&#x27;ll get more than a few hundred flashes by letting the unit adequately cool down both between grid treatments and before turning it completely off.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Efficacy&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;While I would love to say that this unit is perfect, it isn&#x27;t.  If you have course dark hair and light enough skin to activate the unit, then you may see great results.  If you have blonde, red, grey, white or thin dark or medium hair, your mileage may vary.  That means, you may not see the results you expect.  IPL does work for the proper skin type, hair color and thickness, it&#x27;s just that this is a home unit and you shouldn&#x27;t expect miracles.  It also takes several treatments to see results, so don&#x27;t expect to see anything after one treatment.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The one thing I will say for this unit is that it seems to slow hair growth in the treated areas for my skin. I don&#x27;t see the hairs falling out as promised, but I am still hopeful that with enough treatments that may still happen.  I also haven&#x27;t seen any negative effects on my skin as a result of using the unit (no burns or discoloration).  Each flash, though, feels hot for just a moment and then subsides.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Keep in mind that this is a home unit.  The [[ASIN:B005CHHO4Q Remington I-Light Pro Replacement Cartridges]] are around $20-25 each which is likely cheaper than an IPL session from a local business (and definitely cheaper than laser sessions) especially considering you can usually get at least 2.5 sessions out of one lamp cartridge.  The cartridges are also easy to replace.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Strength of flash&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The iLight allows you to adjust the strength of each flash from 1 star (default) to 5 stars.  If you have course dark hair and light skin, 1 star is probably enough.  If you have lighter hair (or deeper roots), you may need to increase the strength up to 5 stars.  As a result of increasing the strength of the flash, this likely reduces the number of flashes as well.  So, I&#x27;m thinking that the possible 1500 flashes is from a unit that is properly cooled and is using 1 star for its entire lifetime. Increasing the strength and not cooling the unit properly seems to drastically reduce bulb lifetime.  If you want to increase the bulb life, you will need to allow the unit to cool and use the least amount of flash strength needed to get the desired result.  So, you should probably start your treatments with 1 star strength and see how that goes for several sessions before increasing the strength.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Moisturizing prior to your session&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you moisturize your skin prior to your sessions, this may help the unit work better.  The unit needs to get the light to the root of each follicle to stop its growth.  Dry skin can prevent the light from penetrating.  Moisturized skin allows the light to penetrate better.  However, don&#x27;t moisturize immediately before the start of a session.  Instead, moisturize and then wait until the lotion has dissipated and the skin is dry to the touch before starting any sessions.  You don&#x27;t want your skin to be wet with a moisturizer when beginning a session for several reasons.  First, it may cause skin reactions. Second, the lotion will smear up the lens in the flash gun (which needs to be cleaned periodically anyway) and the unclean lens will prevent the flash from working effectively.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Smell&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One additional point, while doing each session, expect the smell of burning hair.  This unit creates a very hot short flash which creates this burning smell with each flash.  So, if you don&#x27;t like this smell or don&#x27;t want to smell up your room, you might want to do your sessions outside or in a well ventilated environment.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Rating&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m rating this unit 3 stars for a the following reasons.  First, the touted 1500 flashes from one cartridge isn&#x27;t realistic.  You can only get this number under perfect laboratory conditions.  The best I&#x27;ve been able to achieve is about 300-400 at most letting the unit cool between sessions.  Remington needs to be more realistic with the longevity of the cartridges.  Second, the unit inadequately cools the flash lamp leading to early lamp failure based on Remington&#x27;s suggested usage. Remington has a great idea, but it&#x27;s executed in a mediocre way.  If it had been more thoughtfully designed, I would give this unit more stars.  That said, it is a home unit, so you can&#x27;t expect perfection.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m not saying this unit doesn&#x27;t work or isn&#x27;t effective.  It does work.  But, its effectiveness is limited by the type and thickness of the hair. Note that there is another technique which can be used with the iLight (IPL) that may make it twice as effective even on blond, red or white hair follicles.  I am going to try this technique and report back.  If this technique works, I will raise the star rating on this unit and include this technique.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Updated: 5/3/2012&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have another problem that just surfaced today.  The cord connecting the flash gun to the base now has a broken cable inside it.  When the thick cable is moved into a certain position, the flash gun loses power.  The gun must now be moved into specific positions for the wire to make contact. Once a broken cable happens, it&#x27;s will only get worse. This is clearly a warranty problem at this point, but it also shows that this unit is definitely not that well made.  I have only used the iLight 8-10 times since I&#x27;ve gotten it and I&#x27;m not rough with it at all.  There is no reason that cable should be this fragile. What I would suggest to Remington is to use a cable that is removable on both ends (from the handle and from the base).  If the cable dies, you don&#x27;t have to replace the whole unit.  On this unit, the cable that wires the flash gun is permanently anchored to both the gun and the base.  So, there&#x27;s no way to replace the gun or the cable.trength and not cooling the unit properly seems to drastically reduce bulb lifetime.  If you want to increase the bulb life, you will need to allow the unit to cool and use the least amount of flash strength needed to get the desired result.  So, you should probably start your treatments with 1 star strength and see how that goes for several sessions before increasing the strength.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Moisturizing prior to your session&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you moisturize your skin prior to your sessions, this may help the unit work better. Instead, moisturize and then wait until the lotion has dissipated and the skin is dry to the touch before starting any sessions.  You don&#x27;t want your skin to be wet with a moisturizer when beginning a session for several reasons.  First, it may cause skin reactions. Second, the lotion will smear up the lens in the flash gun (which needs to be cleaned periodically anyway) and the unclean lens will prevent the flash from working effectively.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Smell&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One additional point, while doing each session, expect the smell of burning hair. So, if you don&#x27;t like this smell or don&#x27;t want to smell up your room, you might want to do your sessions outside or in a well ventilated environment.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Rating&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m rating this unit 3 stars for a the following reasons.  First, the touted 1500 flashes from one cartridge isn&#x27;t realistic.  You can only get this number under perfect laboratory conditions.  The best I&#x27;ve been able to achieve is about 300-400 at most letting the unit cool between sessions.  Remington needs to be more realistic with the longevity of the cartridges.  Second, the unit inadequately cools the flash lamp leading to early lamp failure based on Remington&#x27;s suggested usage. Remington has a great idea, but it&#x27;s executed in a mediocre way.  If it had been more thoughtfully designed, I would give this unit more stars.  That said, it is a home unit, so you can&#x27;t expect perfection.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m not saying this unit doesn&#x27;t work or isn&#x27;t effective.  It does work.     <li> I had my legs, underarms and upper-lip professionally lasered 4 years ago, so I know how painful salon lasering is. It took 18 treatments (every 6 weeks) over a 2 year period at a cost of around $4000, which was also painful, but it was worth every penny and all of the excrutiating pain (I am not kidding - every pulse felt like someone had pulled back a large rubber band as far as it could go and then let it snap). I wore yoga pants for two days after each session because my skin was tender and swollen and felt like it was badly sunburnt, but the results were absolutely worth it! About a year ago I started epilating my hairy arms and wishing that I had had them done at the same time as my legs, and now that the Brazilian wax is the thing to do, I wish I had had my whole bikini area done, although I don&#x27;t know if I could tolerate that pain, honestly. I also have to pull anywhere from 20 to 70 hairs a DAY from my chin, and it has gotten so bad that I decided to give the Light Pro a shot. It is less than the cost of one session, so I figured that it was worth the risk of it not working.  Let me say that I am fair-skinned and very dark-haired, so I am the ideal candidate for laser. I wouldn&#x27;t necessarily presume that this works as well for lighter-haired people. My hair grows extraordinarily fast - I was epilating my arms every 5 days and I have already stated that my little black chin-whiskers were popping up daily. This does say not to use on the face, but I figured that if the salon could do it then so could I so I disregarded the warning, and it has been fine except for a few bumps the next day that go away in a few days.   I got the Light Pro about 3 weeks ago and used it immediately. I used the highest setting (which I would recommend, as you get 1000 flashes per bulb regardless of the intensity that you use, so you might as well be as effective as possible)and overlapped even though it says not to. The pain is only a fraction of the salon laser, so I was pretty skeptical as to its effectiveness, but I still kept at it. Rather than wait two weeks as the instructions tell you, I waited two days and did it again, and then I epilated, since my hairs were so long at that point that I had to wear long sleeves. I waited about a week and then treated all areas again, although I did not see any improvement at this point and fully expected that before the month was up I would be packing it up and trying to get Amazon to refund my $250. A week and a day later I started on my 3rd treatment. I finished my chin and arms and was a few pulses into my bikini area when the thing started beeping and stopped delivering pulses. I re-read the manual and realized that my cartridge was used up, which kind of pissed me off because it claimed to have enough flashes to cover the entire body for 3 sessions, and I had only gotten 2 and a half of just my chin, arms, and bikini area, but I did overlap to cover every centimeter of the skin I was treating, so...  I discovered that another cartridge would cost $25, and decided not to waste any more $ on this project when it occurred to me that my bikini area is now very patchy. It is definitely at least 30% less dense. It also occurred to me that I hadn&#x27;t pulled more than 10 or 15 hairs from my chin in a single day in the past week. Hmmm...maybe I should hold off on the refund thing. I epilated my arms that night (Wed), and it is now Sunday night and my hair growth is barely noticible, and what has grown back is very fine and thin. So I ordered another cartridge this morning, because at this rate I believe that I will have hair-free arms and a hair free bikini area by summer, although it may take two more cartridges. Still, the machine plus 2 cartridges is still about $85 less than a single session at the salon, so it is WELL worth the cost!   To sum it up, don&#x27;t be discouraged because you don&#x27;t see immediate results. Give it two treatments and I thing you will notice significant changes in your hair growthand density, but do expect that it will cost you a few $25 cartridges along with the initial cost of the machine, especially if you are doing your legs.</li>
    <li> ***Update #1 (04/23/2012)********************&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have used my i-light pro to treat my legs, bikini area and underarms 3 times. Despite the advice on the box, I have used it to treat my chin 5 to 6 times. I am very happy with the results. I am not seeing 100% results but I did not expect them. I have had professional laser treatments many times in the past for my underarms, bikini area and chin. I have had amazing results with those treatments but as many of you are aware...the expense of professional treatments is not cheap. I have desperately been wanting to treat my legs for years. I bought the Remington i-Light Pro 2 weeks ago (Ulta had a 20% off coupon...so I was able to purchase this product for $200 instead of $250).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The product is easy to use and has easy to understand instructions. The product was carefully designed to keep safety as the #1 priority. I did not experience any problems with the machine as other users have described. After using the i-Light Pro, it would be safe to say that the level of discomfort is nowhere near as significant as professional treatments. I used the highest setting for my treatments. This is probably because professional machines have higher levels of laser penetration...therefore, higher level of results. Products for home use will never deliver professional results or intensity.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It has been 1 1/2 weeks since my first treatment. One thing to keep in mind when purchasing products like this or having professional treatments....HAIR WILL ALWAYS GROW BACK no matter what you are promised. My professional treatments had amazing results, it has been approx 6 years since I had my underarms treated. When my treatments were complete, I probably had 5 to 6 hairs that continued to grow (which I just plucked instead of shaving)...since then I now have probably 50 to 60 hairs that grow. The hairs that were treated did not come back, new hairs have appeared. This is due to hormonal changes...amongst many other reasons (ie. medications).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Considering I have only completed one treatment, I am very happy with my results. The price of the machine itself is less than one professional treatment. It is worth a shot. Even if this machine only provides me with 50% reduction of hair growth, I would say it was worth the money.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I will post updates to my review periodically to keep you posted.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;m refraining from a 5 star review for 2 simple reasons: only when my treatments have been completed and I can assess the long-term results will I be able to definitely give it an extra star or not. I can&#x27;t remember the last time I have been compelled to write a review so early, and so enthusiastically! When it comes to hair removal products, feeling enthusiastic about any one of the thousands out there is very rare indeed. As someone who bought the Tria a year ago for the ridiculous price of $495 with very high hopes and expectations, my experience with that product was abhorrent. I gave it a 1 star review due to its terrible flaws and for the simple fact that it did not work for me AT ALL. If I could give it a 0 I would. After the endless hours invested and multiple treatments I had nothing to show for it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I had several salon IPL sessions done on my chest and stomach in 2005 which cost me something like $1200. I decided to stop the treatments due to this high cost and because at that point I was satisfied enough with the results I got which were impressive: at least a 60-65% reduction in hair which throughout the years since has remained permanent. So I begin my treatments with the experience of having had IPL treatments done in the past and with less than half the hair I had naturally. I completed my first session the day after I received the I-light Pro, and I used the highest setting from the start (which I recommend, unless your pain tolerance is very low). The pain was quite reminiscent of the salon treatments I had, which I took as a good sign--if you feel nothing when you zap that means you either have no hair in the area or thehair is too fine for the follicle to absorb the light and be killed. Over time, as you lose hair (too soon to make any conclusions about long term permanence) treatments will be far less painful as there is less hair to zap.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Nevertheless having the Tria experience in mind I didn&#x27;t let myself get too happy since those treatments were also painful but in the end nothing happened. Immediately and in the days after the treatment nothing looked different, the hair began to grow like after any shave--this is normal. It was on or about the ten-day mark that something remarkable happened: after taking off a t-shirt I noticed on the inside tons of little hairs! This was exactly what happened to the hair after the salon treatments at $250 a pop. The dead hair gets ejected from your skin. It&#x27;s working! At the 2 week mark, I can see new bald spots where those little hairs have fallen out. I can confidently say that after a single treatment close to 20% of the hair on my chest and stomach has disappeared and another large percentage of hairs have thinned out (or perhaps the new spareness giving that illusion.) I am simply in awe of this product. The price, the ergonomics (mostly), the larger zap area, the convenience and ultimately the results make this in my opinion the holy grail of at home laser hair removal.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Unfortunately 1/4 of the way into my second treatment the IPL cartridge gave in, so I would hope Remington starts to impose some quality control on these cartridges. If you want close to hair free results, it will take more than 3 treatments--it could take up to 6 or 8 or even 10 depending on an individual&#x27;s hair. But that is okay. This product works, and is far faster and efficient in covering all your areas. I never imagined back when I was doing salon treatments that one day I could buy my own machine for less the price of one session and do it myself with actual results. Amazing.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE 2/24/2013:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I completely forgot abouthaving written this review so I didn&#x27;t get the chance to update based on further usage. So after using the product several more times, including a long months-long pause (I went on vacation and got a deep tan) and then once again doing about 2 more sessions after re-starting I&#x27;m going to have to lower my review by one star. I had higher hopes for the product but in the end it&#x27;s quite clear that this is not a permanent solution. What it is though, is a very effective temporary reduction solution. In my experience I would have to say that you could do 10 sessions to the T and you will still not get *permanent* hair loss results--what it will do is put a huge amount of your hair follicles in some kind of dormant mode--and I&#x27;ll gladly say that this is a decent outcome. The results can last for months and months. You will have so much less hair for such a long time that any grooming you may have to do will be significantly reduced. So in the end, this product is a disappointment in one respect (expecting salon laser-like permanent results) but on the other hand I wouldn&#x27;t characterize its temporary results as a waste of time either, since the temporary nature of the results actually do last a long time--which makes shaving whatever is left a breeze until you see that you need a maintenance session to put the hair to sleep once again. It is still a much much much better value for money than the piece of garbage that is the TRIA. One word of advice that bears repeating: use it on the highest setting from the start. Using the lower settings becomes that much more of a waste considering there&#x27;s no permanent loss.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My hope is that over the next few years Remington or other companies will improve these systems by increasing the longevity of the cartridges, reduction of noise and heat, larger zap area, and most important of all increase the energy output of the light/laser in order to cause permanent hair loss.</li>

The whole head is not the zapper, but a small window on the head. Not that bit of an issue: just go over those the next time. Eventually they will go away.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Things I have not tested:&lt;br /&gt;I used it only on a small area, less than 25 zaps per session. I have no way to advise on the longevity of the bulb.&lt;br /&gt;Long term, I do not know if the hair will regrow. It&#x27;s now been 4 months and seems ok, though. If the hairs grow back, I would still use it again.here there are contours, and probably missed due to the small zapping window.&lt;br /&gt;Underarm: Maybe 50% less.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Week 7-10:&lt;br /&gt;Stepped up the underarm to every 3 days.&lt;br /&gt;Chin is pretty well clear except for stragglers here and there.&lt;br /&gt;Underarm showing definite difference from other side, now.&lt;br /&gt;Breakouts are pretty much gone from my face near the zapped areas.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Results:&lt;br /&gt;It works.&lt;br /&gt;None of the Cons below are deal breakers in the least.     <li> I have had 10-12 professional laser treatments on my legs(full leg and bikini) which cost a good deal and have had pretty decent results considering what I started out with. It used to take me 15 minutes to shave my full legs and the tub would be covered with hair. Now i can shave 2-3xweek and the hair is finer. I am by no means hairless after all those professional treatments. hair growth is dependent on genetics and follicle sensitivity to testosterone/DHT in both men and women. Hormone levels will fluctuate throughout your lifetime and theses changes can reactivate hair follicles and start producing dark hair again. The only way to prevent hair regrowth after treatments is to take MEDICATIONS which block DHT like propecia or spironolactone or bith control pills. I took spiro for 6 months and did laser and had amazing results but drugs have side effects so off the drugs, hair comes back. The ONLY form of permanent hair removal to date is electrolysis and even that can take a year/years and is not good for large areas.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My experience with the Remington is similar to professional laser treatments:the results from the highest setting on the device yield the same results as the lower settings on professional laser.     <li> Let me start off by saying that I have had laser hair removal done professionally so I am familiar with the process.     <li> First off, this hurts like hell on any sensitive area (like the private area lol)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I used this on my arms, the first time on level 2, then 3 more times on level 5.     <li> Thusfar I have had pretty good success with this product. At first I was quite disappointed but after a month of using it every other day the hair is actually starting to just randomly fall out.  My skin is quite pale and my hair is a dark brown so I&#x27;m fairly ideal for IPL. I&#x27;m also male, and have really thick coarse hair on my chest and shoulders which is where I mainly used this. Basically I&#x27;m a prime candidate for frying hair haha    A little bit about this product however....  Remington seems to compare it a lot to professional systems, which it should not. Remington did not design this product actually. The original product patent is under Shaser Inc, Shaser Inc was formerly known as Shaser BioScience.  Shaser BioScience originally designed this as a 3rd party consultation separate from Remington and Spectrum Brands. Spectrum currently owns Shaser BioScience, known just as Shaser Inc now.  To add another twist to the tale Shaser Inc. currently has a lawsuit opened against it by Dr. Harvey Jay, a doctor whom has specialized in laser therapy for a number of things, in this particular case, hair removal.    The patents owned by Dr. Jay discussing the technology behind low-energy IPL are: US Patent  #6,824,542, # 6,916,316, #7,175,617, #7,553,308, and #8,393,330  The patents owned by Shaser Inc. discussing the actual product itself are: US D670397 S1 and US 8,480,721, among about 22 other language translations and variations    The reason I mention patents is because they reveal a huge quantity of information about this system and some really shifty advertising scams by Remington.  The hair reduction of 48% after 6 months that Remington quotes is from Smith et al. in the journal &#x27;Lasers in Medical Surgery&#x27;, titled \\&quot;Long-term results of hair photo-epilation\\&quot; published 1998.  I could not find any study done by Remington at all and the numbers coincidentally match up to the decimal so I assume that&#x27;s the study they quote. That was done using professional systems of course, and it was done over 15 years ago.    A little bit more about the patents.... In Dr. Jay&#x27;s patents he further explains that follicular damage is an UNINTENDED side effect of low-energy IPL. Any permanent removal is actually an accident and the system is designed not to do it. I&#x27;ll give a direct quote from Dr. Jay&#x27;s patents:  \\&quot;Thus, in contrast to prior methods, which are aimed at completely destroying the hair follicle, the present method contemplates only a partial destruction of the follicles or, alternatively, a destruction of the hair inside the follicles. In either case, the hair will grow and again appear on the treated surface in the absence of additional controlled light application\\&quot;    Now even more about the patents.... The nice thing about Remington not having actually designed this system but instead only facilitating the sale of it is that it&#x27;s quite easy to \\&quot;hack\\&quot; the machine. The little EEPROM chip inside every replacement xenon flash tube contains current # of flashes, total flashes, manufacturing date, and initial energy of the lamp.  The machine dynamically adapts the energy to the lamp, theoretically you could solder any xenon flash tube and the machine dynamically adapts to determine the required voltage and capacitance to output light. Very neat system actually. I was more impressed by that then what the product was actually intended to do since that&#x27;s actually some really complicated circuitry haha  You can hack the little EEPROM chip and as long as you leave a minimum of one property about the lamp then the system will run. You can wipe the flash count, energy, etc. and just leave the manufacturing date and you can get unlimited flashes (or at least until the bulb explodes). I just used Bus Pirate v3 to modify the eeprom chip, it&#x27;s a DS2431, one of the simplest EEPROM chips out there, very easy to read and modify. It can be modified by either bus pirate v3+, a raspberry pi, or an arduino fairly easily.  But if you do that be warned thateventually the bulb will literally explode. It&#x27;s housed fairly safe inside the machine so no glass really gets anywhere but if you&#x27;re scared of light bulbs exploding then don&#x27;t mess with the flash count.    The system is set to do 4 pulses of 7ms length at 3.5 Joules each, 3ms delay between pulses giving a total of 7 J/cm^2  The J/cm^2 is a value you will never see outside the pseudoscientific realm that is hair removal. In reality it&#x27;s 7 Watts of power not 7 Joules, a joule is a watt-second but you drop the second due to multiplying by the frequency hence giving watts... But anyway,The actual output is 14-16W of power. Due to the machines ability to dynamically adapt and the EEPROM containing modifications to energy output for each individual replacement bulb, Remington rated the system as between 7-8J/cm^2, meaning you&#x27;ll get between 14-16J (err... watts) in the 1x2cm filter window applied to your skin.    The pulse duration tends to burn the cathode and cause blackening of the tube because they use a very low quality xenon flash tube. Theoretically a good quality xenon flash tube at 7ms pulse duration should be able to survive 50,000+ pulses, sometimes even up to 1,000,000 if it&#x27;s a very good quality bulb. By good quality I mean a $4 bulb haha.  Xenon flash tubes that small aren&#x27;t exactly expensive. Remington really went out of their way to make sure you got a terrible product, I have no idea how they even managed to find such a horrible quality bulb. These bulbs do appear to be able to survive up to about 5000-6000 flashes from my experience thusfar before they simply explode or crack.    Also, in Dr. Jay&#x27;s patents he recommended between 5J/cm^2 to 40J/cm^2 of energy output to achieve satisfactory results, meaning for this system it is on the low end of that scale. He recommended 20J/cm^2 for people of coloured skin and the 40J/cm^2 for light skinned people. Those values would still only give temporary removal as well, it would not result in permanent follicle damage.    Now.... after all that rambling, did it work? Yes it seems to have removed my hair. Some of it still grows but a good portion has been removed.  Is it permanent? Well according to everything written about the technology it would appear to not be. IPL and laser themselves are not always permanent and given the low energy of this system it would suggest even more that it is not permanent.  I&#x27;d recommend this if you have a small area that  you want effectively kept hair free, I don&#x27;t think I&#x27;d recommend it for legs or total body hair removal however, you would spend a fortune on bulb replacements.  I gave it 3/5 because the price to quality just isn&#x27;t there. You&#x27;re paying a lot of money for what is essentially a glorified strobe light with a very poor quality and weak bulb that they slap a $5 700nm cutoff filter onto the front of and put it in a nice box. Then since they&#x27;re so nice to you after you&#x27;ve handed them over $200 for the unit, they&#x27;ve developed a way to really grab your money with the low flash count on the bulbs which they charge a huge markup on.  It&#x27;s up to you whether you think this system is worth the price to replace waxing or shaving, you&#x27;ll still need to shave much of the hair off since it can&#x27;t get all of it of course. If you did your complete body and didn&#x27;t mess around with the unit to unlock more flashes than I could easily see you using 5-6 bulbs/year, depending on how hairy you are I suppose. I had to flash every 2-4 days for the first month to see any real noticeable decrease in hair and I&#x27;m still flashing it about once a week and still need to shave many portions that this thing just can&#x27;t seem to deal with despite the dark hair.</li>
    <li> Women .. this is it! Facial hair - GONE! The magic takes place with just 4 sessions! I  bought it last year and it worked like magic on chin-hair.     <li> For the last ten years, I have been an adult woman struggling with unwanted facial hair. I am mixed race with light skin, but the hairs on my chin and throat are thick, wiry, and black. A decade ago, it was just a few hairs, but as of five years ago, it was enough that I had to switch to shaving, partly to save time, and partly to reduce the number of ingrown hairs that would result. These ingrown hairs have to be dug out in order to be removed, and have caused many blemishes. Furthermore, it&#x27;s painful and embarrassing. I try to avoid well-lit places, I keep my head down even when I laugh, and I won&#x27;t let myself be seen without makeup. I even tried to avoid having anyone touch my face for fear they would feel my bristly five o&#x27;clock shadow. I have despaired over this, felt helpless, powerless, and miserable over it. I have felt constantly ashamed at having to shave my face like a man. Honestly, it made me feel like less of woman and my self-esteem (never amazing to begin with) has suffered.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I could never afford laser treatments at the salon, and I had heard that some mixed race skin tones were too dark, anyway. When I first heard about it, I considered NoNo, but only until I read the terrible reviews. Finally, a commercial for the Tria home laser changed my life (bear with me here, I know this is a review for the Remington). I never dreamed that something at home could work for me or my skin/hair type, but I did my research anyway. The reviews for the Tria were good, mostly, but more than a few people mentioned the Remington Pro IPL, and that it worked as well if not better, was less expensive, and had been on the market for a few years. I pored over the reviews (thank you TheRealWoman!!!), and despite the fact that the product is not recommended for the face, many, many customers confessed to using it there with amazing results. Just like that, I went from feeling like I had a guilty secret to hide from the world, to feeling like I was part of a community; on top of that, while I didn&#x27;t want to build up my hopes too much, I dreamed of being close to a solution to what I had dubbed The Nightmare of My Life.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have used the Remington on my freshly shaven face, on the Level 3 setting, every other day for a month now. In order to really gauge light bulb life, I have used it exclusively on my primary problem areas, my chin and neck and (slight) mustache. I have also taken advice from other reviewers: I clean the laser window frequently, and give it 3-4 seconds in-between pulses to keep the bulb from overheating. I don&#x27;t know if it helps, but it makes sense. Each session is approximately 40-50 pulses and takes me approximately 15 minutes, and so far I am still using the original bulb.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;At first I didn&#x27;t detect any changes, but now, in my fourth week, I can see major progress. I don&#x27;t need to do my mustache area anymore. To be fair, it was never plentiful or thick, but now you can no longer see the hair follicles or any growth. I am going to stop treating it and see if/when it grows back. Now my neck and chin...other reviewers reported noticeable results at two weeks. After four weeks, I can feel and see the difference. In the morning, before I shave, I feel fewer hairs. I still shave every day because I still have growth, but I believe this has a lot to do with growth cycles. I have had many ingrown hairs that I had to tweeze even while the majority were shaved off, so my growth cycle is currently all over the map. While I still do the whole area, it&#x27;s starting to become apparent that hair is only growing noticeably in patches, mostly in the same places where I had frequent ingrown hairs.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I cannot describe how incredible these results feel. If you&#x27;ve struggled with facial hair as a woman, you know how much it undermines your confidence, your enjoyment of life, your spontaneity. I feel like I can go camping again! Better yet, I feel like I can wake up next to someone and not run for the bathroom and the razor. I&#x27;m getting my life back and it feels absolutely amazing. (One more word about the price tag: If you&#x27;re considering buying this, do it. I know I didn&#x27;t mention it, but the price really scared me off, even though it was considerably cheaper than the Tria. But when I thought about what I would pay to be free of this nightmare, what I would pay for this to work, I realized the amount is a pittance. So far, I&#x27;m over the moon. If it continues like this/gets better, then that&#x27;s the bee&#x27;s knees. I can&#x27;t believe I didn&#x27;t buy this sooner! I use level five (the highest) all the time. This is about one-tenth of the pain of epilation (I&#x27;ve tried an epilator a few times, and I always quit after a few square inches, because the pain is much too intense). The description of a rubber band flicking the skin somewhat fits, but there is definitely some brief feeling of heat as well. If you&#x27;ve ever had wax dripped onto you, each time you press the button feels like that sensation, but only for a very brief split second, and then the pain is gone.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The treatment window is narrow, and it is a bit hard to tell what you&#x27;ve already zapped sometimes. Fortunately, it does seem to cause a mild redness around the follicle (which has lasted up to two days) so that helps to see where you&#x27;ve zapped. But I definitely do miss spots.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I am on my second (first replacement) bulb. Interestingly, the directions say the bulb maintains at least 90% of its intensity for the full 1500 flashes, but in fact, I found that when I changed bulbs, there was a dark appearance to half of the bulb I took out, as if it had been partially burned out, and the new replacement bulb was much stronger than the bulb I had just replaced. If you are spending this sort of money, I recommend always keeping a back-up bulb handy, in case your bulb has some unexpected problems. It seems from the other reviews like that is pretty common.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Anyhow, I didn&#x27;t really notice much results until about 7-10 days after my second session. Then, it was obvious that this thing was working. Nine weeks in, I&#x27;d say 70-80% of my hair is either completely gone or so fine as to be irrelevant, and I started out with coarse hair and a lot of it. I usually shave twice a week now, just to clean up the leftover hairs a bit, but even if I go a week without shaving, the hair is fine enough that it is not unpleasant. Shaving used to be unpleasant when so much coarse hair would start to grow back, but now, it is not a bother at all.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I don&#x27;t know how long the results are going to last, but I do know that this is less painful than epilation or waxing, and probably at least as durable. And cheaper than laser by a good bit. So no, it isn&#x27;t perfect, but for light skin and dark hair, it is definitely the best option out there, and it has been well worth the purchase price in terms of the fun it has been to have a hairless front. If this product wasn&#x27;t out there, I&#x27;d just choose to be hairy.</li>

Laser, or IPL can at best promise PERMANENT HAIR REDUCTION and that&#x27;s only if 1) you have the right skin type, 2) you have dark enough hair and 3) you manage to hit the hair during the right growth cycle in order to \\&quot;damage\\&quot; it. Tip: read about the three phases of hair growth to understand why you have to \\&quot;zap\\&quot; it in the ANAGEN growth phase.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve had a facial hair problem since my teens and I&#x27;ve tried everything on the market from bleach (imagine being told from a boy in middle school that your bleached-blonde moustache makes you look like Hulk Hogan), to hair removal cream, to electrolysis, to laser, to plucking and finally, in my 30s, I just starting shaving it because it was easy and cheap. Here&#x27;s how:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- They used it on the lowest setting&lt;br /&gt;- They allowed the flash cartridge to properly cool between flashes (as in, not flash constantly for minutes on end like some people who are in a rush may do)&lt;br /&gt;- They tested it in a properly ventilated room to prevent premature overheating.&lt;br /&gt;- They tested it under PERFECTLY CLEAN AND DUST FREE CONDITIONS.&lt;br /&gt;- The flash bulb test was NOT done while being used on someone&#x27;s skin hence the lens was never dirty during the test and which did not lead to added heat building up in the unit (The lens DOES get dirty very quickly even after 5 or 6 flashes).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So doing it like this, I can see how Remington&#x27;s test facility got 1500 flashes out of the cartridge. Now then; Here is why I think the cartridges aren&#x27;t lasting 1500 flashes.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- People are using it on the highest setting all the time (obviously it&#x27;s gonna impact the life of the flash bulb no matter what people here will tell you)&lt;br /&gt;- People are using it in a poorly kept environment i.e. dusty room from pet dander, pet hair, smoking (dust accumulates on the lens and bulb itself and negatively impact its lifespan)&lt;br /&gt;- People are using it in a hot/humid room&lt;br /&gt;- People are NOT keeping the lens clean during treatment sessions and in between flashes.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So folks, when you use it, make time for the session so that you&#x27;re not in a rush. Do the treatment in a clean, cool and dust free environment.     <li> 2013.03.14 So far 95 % of my arm and leg hair is gone. In areas where the hair is courser like the bikini area it&#x27;s down by 60% and facial hair is down by 35%. I have to send my unit in for warranty repair because flexing the cable makes it not work at times or cause the panel lights to flash.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2013.02.05: 3rd session. Looking at my hair prior to treating it I noticed that about 50% of my arm and 30% of my leg hair isn&#x27;t growing back now. Pubic hair maybe 20% reduced. It seems that the courser the hair is the more resistant it is. I&#x27;m keeping tabs on lamp life using my tips listed below which so far are working by preventing the lamp from overheating. Read \\&quot;Extending Lamp Life\\&quot; below.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2013.01.18: I&#x27;m on my 2nd session which didn&#x27;t make it halfway before the lamp wore out. It doesn&#x27;t seem to last more than a few hundred flashes (not that I counted them). Could it be shipping damage? Dunno. I&#x27;ll do some sample counting next time to estimate the number of flashes when the new lamps come. I think it might be my rapid fire use of it the first session that wore the lamp out faster. It did get quite warm but not to kick into overheat mode. In a couple places I have to turn it back to 3 so it didn&#x27;t sting so much. The only thing I notice at this early stage is a bit of itching or irritation in spots. I&#x27;ll see what happens in the next month...&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Original: I tried my first small session today and my impression is that it&#x27;s plenty powerful enough and the unit build quality looks great. I wound up using level 4 and 5 with my pale skin and brown hair. Mostly it felt like a pinch with heat flash but a couple spots felt more like a shock and probably because of more hair follicles. They say that the higher the level you can stand the better it takes the hair out. Of course I&#x27;m judging the correct level by how each flash should typically feel as well as noticing if the skin is not being adversely harmed. After the session I don&#x27;t feel any discomfort or notice any redness or injury at all on the treated areas.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve read some of the low star reviews before buying as I will do but many seem verging on hysteria, conspiracy, or don&#x27;t know how to use the thing. If you&#x27;re going to write a review good or bad keep it factual and sober otherwise it appears that you&#x27;re making it up.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;IMPORTANT!: As the manual said, pull the nose off and check the lamp cart in case it came loose in shipping. Mine was loose and one pin was misaligned so I bent it straight and the cart seated in snugly. If I hadn&#x27;t read that in the manual the unit wouldn&#x27;t have worked.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ll update this review and star rating as I go with how it performs over the months...&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Extending Lamp Life&lt;br /&gt;Some people complaint about short lamp life, which I too have experienced. I don&#x27;t think it&#x27;s a good design as far as keeping the lamp cool and the heat eventually makes it fail prematurely. My advise is to slow down how fast you flash the unit so that the flash tube stays cooler and doesn&#x27;t fracture from overheating and don&#x27;t block the air vents of the hand piece. I&#x27;m keeping the flash intervals at greater than 4 seconds with rest periods of a minute if I feel any little amount of warmth of the air venting out of the hand unit. Using a longer flash interval of probably 6 - 8 seconds would probably be okay for continuous use. Never get impatient and start flashing it fast for little stint, that could be all you need to overheat the tube. Leave the unit on and fan running if you take breaks in your session. Every bit of cooling will help. From my experience I think you&#x27;ll be able to extend the lamp&#x27;s life but it will still fail prematurely due to lots of tiny heat cracks forming in the tube to a point where they leak. My current lamp I estimate is getting close to it&#x27;s maximum flash count using a 4 to 6 second flash interval but it still has developed a fine tangle of tiny fractures all around the cathode but none big enough to fail.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In a nutshell the problem lies in the way the reflectors in front and behind the tube shroud it from the cooling air so it doesn&#x27;t cool very fast because no real airflow is happening within the confines of the reflectors to cool the center section of the tube. It&#x27;s a shame such a great product has this flaw, but at least it can be partially worked around. This unit really should have been designed with a much higher airflow to cool the lamp and maybe have incorporated some heatsinking.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Other Tips to Extend the Lamp Life&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1, I keep cotton swabs and isopropyl alcohol on hand while using the unit, to clean the vaporized debris off of the lens whenever anything is seen on it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2, Between uses pull the hand unit nose off and see if the back of the lens and reflective surfaces are clean and shiny. Also look at the lamp&#x27;s reflector. It may develop a haze on it. To clean that off I remove the lamp. hold it over a sink and have a small spray bottle with isopropyl alcohol in it that I spray the reflector and tube with. Then I carefully shake the alcohol off and use a hair dryer to dry the lamp off.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Why the Lamp Fails (The technical version)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Xenon flash tube inside of the lamp if overheated develops small fractures that allow the gas inside to seep out. The cracks occur right around the tip of the cathode electrode which is the larger of the two inside the tube and the one that will heat up greatly since that&#x27;s where the arcing starts. The intense blast of the arc and heat build up eventual causes the nearby quartz tube glass to fail.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So other than the tube failing how does the unit know when the lamp has \\&quot;expired\\&quot; at 1,500 flashes? Well when I had the lamp apart I noticed a little \\&quot;transistor\\&quot; inside. I looked up the part number an it turns out to be a serially programmed EEPROM. Basically a tiny bit of memory that can store a number. The unit reads the number when turned on adds how many flashes you use and then loads the new number count back into that EEPROM. Apparently Remington deems the lamp&#x27;s power level to be deteriorated enough at 1,500 flashes that it&#x27;s out of spec as far as maintaining performance.o fail.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In a nutshell the problem lies in the way the reflectors in front and behind the tube shroud it from the cooling air so it doesn&#x27;t cool very fast because no real airflow is happening within the confines of the reflectors to cool the center section of the tube. It&#x27;s a shame such a great product has this flaw, but at least it can be partially worked around. This unit really should have been designed with a much higher airflow to cool the lamp and maybe have incorporated some heatsinking.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Other Tips to Extend the Lamp Life&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1, I keep cotton swabs and isopropyl alcohol on hand while using the unit, to clean the vaporized debris off of the lens whenever anything is seen on it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2, Between uses pull the hand unit nose off and see if the back of the lens and reflective surfaces are clean and shiny. Also look at the lamp&#x27;s reflector. It may develop a haze on it. To clean that off I remove the lamp. hold it over a sink and have a small spray bottle with isopropyl alcohol in it that I spray the reflector and tube with. Then I carefully shake the alcohol off and use a hair dryer to dry the lamp off.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Why the Lamp Fails (The technical version)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Xenon flash tube inside of the lamp if overheated develops small fractures that allow the gas inside to seep out. The cracks occur right around the tip of the cathode electrode which is the larger of the two inside the tube and the one that will heat up greatly since that&#x27;s where the arcing starts. The intense blast of the arc and heat build up eventual causes the nearby quartz tube glass to fail.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So other than the tube failing how does the unit know when the lamp has \\&quot;expired\\&quot; at 1,500 flashes? Well when I had the lamp apart I noticed a little \\&quot;transistor\\&quot; inside. I looked up the part number an it turns out to be a serially programmed EEPROM. Basically a tiny bit of memory that can store a number. The unit reads the number when turned on adds how many flashes you use and then loads the new number count back into that EEPROM. Apparently Remington deems the lamp&#x27;s power level to be deteriorated enough at 1,500 flashes that it&#x27;s out of spec as far as maintaining performance.</li>
    <li> So I have PCOS which means I&#x27;m way harrier than I would like. The light is attracted to the dark hair follicle and basically burns it enough over time that it pretty much dies and the hair doesn&#x27;t grow anymore or takes a super long time to grow back. So I watched the instructional DVD before I started using it. Sure enough, the model on the DVD was holding the wand still on the skin, zapping, then picking it up and moving it just a bit further before holding it still and zapping again. I have to say the DVD was extremely helpful to me.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Armed with as much information as possible, I was ready to turn it on. The device goes into a test mode and beeps at you until you hold the area of skin you are wanting to zap over the testing scanner. If the area tests well, then the I-Light Pro activates and a green light indicates you are ready to begin. If the area does not test successfully, the I-Light Pro will not activate and you won&#x27;t be able to use it. I am a natural brunette with fair, untanned skin, so I tested well. Naturally dark or tanned skin is not recommended, as is people whose natural hair color is light or grey.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The manual warns not to overlap, so I recommend paying attention to where you begin your work and make sure you keep paying attention as you progress with the I-Light Pro. I used a freckle on each leg as my starting point so I knew where to stop when I reached the freckle again.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;When you turn on the device, it automatically sets itself to the lowest energy setting. I started with the highest energy settings, since that is supposed to be most effective. This was fine on most of my legs, but I had to reduce to the middle energy setting for the area behind my knees. I also used the middle setting for my underarms and bikini area.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Using the device is really easy. You place the end of the wand completely on your skin. If it doesn&#x27;t make a proper contact, it won&#x27;t let you zap that area. The device emits a chirp when a good contact is made and allows you to zap. A working device will not allow you to zap while the wand is in mid-air, for safety reasons.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I did feel a little warmth and occasional tingles as I worked, but it wasn&#x27;t uncomfortable and was over with very quickly.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The instructions say that you should use it once every two weeks for three treatments and then use it as needed. After the first treatment, the hair on my knees didn&#x27;t start growing again for almost two weeks. I&#x27;m not sure the hair on my thighs started regrowing at all, but then the hair there has also grown far slower and finer than anywhere else on my body.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;When I performed the second treatment, I forgot to change the energy setting and used it everywhere on the lowest setting. I realized it later and thought it would be a great feature to make you select an energy level each time you start to prevent using an undesired setting.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have now performed four treatments and can say that I do see a definite decrease in the speed at which my hair grows back although I don&#x27;t see the effect that I&#x27;d hoped for. I don&#x27;t have to shave my thighs at all anymore and shave my knees about every two weeks. My lower legs need to be shaved about once a week. The I-Light Pro seems least effective under my arms, and I have to shave there about twice a week still.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ll be doing a fifth treatment soon and hope that it will be the one that eliminates shaving for a while. I&#x27;ll check back in once I&#x27;ve had time to know for sure.
